  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5ee6a41d-a9c6-4c72-8b36-8044eb3b775a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's a pretty common procedure to change the names in children's books to make them more approachable and easier to read for the target audience. Rüdi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's a pretty common procedure to change the names in children's books to make them more approachable and easier to read for the target audience. Rüdiger would be too difficult for English language readers.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_108666775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108666775" />
    <a title="Barbara (VampAngel)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3902029-barbara-vampangel"><img alt="Barbara (VampAngel)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518910440p2/3902029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108666775?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara (VampAngel)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara (VampAngel)" href="/user/show/3902029-barbara-vampangel">Barbara (VampAngel)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Every children and even adults</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108666775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1389279938772205716">So, I dug up my 1987 beat up copy and I'm rereading it. I had forgotten how cute this was. <span id="freeTextContainer17207503221146696453"><i>I read this so many times I was young. So. Many. Times.</i><br/><br/>The illustrations are still charming and maybe the best part of the whole book? I remembered the illustrations long after I'd forgotten the story itself. <br/><br/>The story is cute, and I can see why it appealed to me when I was young. Tony, a 9-year-old boy, has a vampire (Rudolph) visit his window one night and they become friends. They go on late night adventures, including hanging out at the cemetery; with the help of a magical cape, Tony can fly</span>
  <span id="freeText17207503221146696453" style="display:none"><i>I read this so many times I was young. So. Many. Times.</i><br /><br />The illustrations are still charming and maybe the best part of the whole book? I remembered the illustrations long after I'd forgotten the story itself. <br /><br />The story is cute, and I can see why it appealed to me when I was young. Tony, a 9-year-old boy, has a vampire (Rudolph) visit his window one night and they become friends. They go on late night adventures, including hanging out at the cemetery; with the help of a magical cape, Tony can fly with Rudolph; Rudolph's sister forms a crush on Tony; Tony's parents are very suspicious but ultimately too clueless to figure out what's going on, etc. But the writing itself is so-so. (And I don't think I feel that way just because I'm an adult who expects a different style of writing. I read enough children's books that I know what to expect and how to adjust myself to that mindset, and ultimately, good writing is good writing no matter what the format, what my age, etc.)<br /><br />I think I'll read the second book in the series to make an ultimate decision on the Little Vampire series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17207503221146696453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9030396015705742686">I started reading this with my first grader and then finished it on my own, because I enjoyed the story so much. <br/><br/>Anton (or Tony in the English version) is a third-grader who befriends a young vampire boy in this charming story. They go on adventures together, visit Anton's family vault, go flying with a magic cape, and have a run-in with the new cemetery groundskeeper. I really enjoyed this story. <br/><br/>I was intrigued by the little vampire's name, Rudolph Sackville-Bagg. Now why, I thought, would he </span>
  <span id="freeText9030396015705742686" style="display:none">I started reading this with my first grader and then finished it on my own, because I enjoyed the story so much. <br /><br />Anton (or Tony in the English version) is a third-grader who befriends a young vampire boy in this charming story. They go on adventures together, visit Anton's family vault, go flying with a magic cape, and have a run-in with the new cemetery groundskeeper. I really enjoyed this story. <br /><br />I was intrigued by the little vampire's name, Rudolph Sackville-Bagg. Now why, I thought, would he be named after a disliked branch of hobbits from the world of JRR Tolkien? Turns out that this is simply the English version of his name, and very English it is. I would have much preferred his original, German name, Rüdiger von Schlotterstein. I think we English readers lost out here. <br /><br />Nicely done!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077495836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4520464058623539711">I loved these books when I was young, I used to read them over and over again. I'm sure part of my fascination with vampires as an adult comes from Sommer-Bodenburg's "Little Vampire". Anton is a 9-year old boy who likes horror stories and befriends Rudiger, a vampire who looks about his age. His parents don't believe in vampires and are skeptical about his new friend, while Rudiger's sister, Anna, joins the boys in their adventures. Reading this so many years later, I was not disappointed at al</span>
  <span id="freeText4520464058623539711" style="display:none">I loved these books when I was young, I used to read them over and over again. I'm sure part of my fascination with vampires as an adult comes from Sommer-Bodenburg's "Little Vampire". Anton is a 9-year old boy who likes horror stories and befriends Rudiger, a vampire who looks about his age. His parents don't believe in vampires and are skeptical about his new friend, while Rudiger's sister, Anna, joins the boys in their adventures. Reading this so many years later, I was not disappointed at all. I still found it wonderful, funny, charming and quite unique in its premise. </span>

<div id="review_482595058" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482595058" />
    <a title="sj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4740396-sj"><img alt="sj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384356482p2/4740396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/482595058?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sj" href="/user/show/4740396-sj">sj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781453270448" href="/book/show/15850873-the-little-vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4740396-sj?shelf=childhood-favourites">childhood-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4740396-sj?shelf=egalley">egalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482595058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1405135471369867939">Originally posted <a href='http://wp.me/p1Zgyz-17y' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>Nostalgia ahoy!<br/><br/>I think I was in the third grade the first time I read this book.  In fact, I'm almost positive I was because that was the year that <em>The Lost Boys</em> came out, and I developed my first vampire obsession.  Of course, being in the third grade, I wasn't yet allowed to check books out of the library that would've matched thematically with <em>The Lost Boys</em>, so I made do with what I could find, giving my librarian the elementary school version of the stink eye the entir</span>
  <span id="freeText1405135471369867939" style="display:none">Originally posted <a href="http://wp.me/p1Zgyz-17y" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />Nostalgia ahoy!<br /><br />I think I was in the third grade the first time I read this book.  In fact, I'm almost positive I was because that was the year that <em>The Lost Boys</em> came out, and I developed my first vampire obsession.  Of course, being in the third grade, I wasn't yet allowed to check books out of the library that would've matched thematically with <em>The Lost Boys</em>, so I made do with what I could find, giving my librarian the elementary school version of the stink eye the entire time.<br /><br />Enter <em>My Friend the Vampire</em>, first published auf Deutsch as <em>Der Kleine Vampir</em> in 1979.  That's this book.  I'm not entirely sure why the first US edition had a different name than all the others, and right now I'm too lazy to go digging through the internet to find out.<br /><br />Anyway.  I read the first book and then the next 3 or 4, then lamented the fact that there didn't appear to be anymore books about human boy Tony and his vampire friends Rudolph and Anna.  A few years ago, I decided to go looking for these books, thinking my oldest son would be into them, only to discover that they were out of print and people on the internet want to charge ridiculous amounts of money for them.<br /><br />I sighed with sadness.  Not just because I wasn't willing to spend upwards of 100$ on a book for my kids, but because I learned that there were MANY MORE BOOKS that just hadn't ever made it over to the US.  They were translated into English and sold in the UK, but just never made it over here.<br /><br />AND THEN, late last year, I decided to go looking for them AGAIN when I was writing my own letter to Santa.<br /><br />I was overjoyed to find that this first book was available as an ebook, AND that <a href="http://www.openroadmedia.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Open Road Media</a> was offering it up on <a href="http://netgalley.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">NetGalley</a>.  I pounced.<br /><br />When I was approved, there may have been (okay, there totally was) a squeal of joy.<br /><br />I kind of wanted to put off reading it, though...because what if it wasn't as great as I remembered it being?  It'd been more than 25 years since the first time I read it,  and I'm definitely not the same reader I was then.<br /><br />I was worried for nothing.<br /><br />Not only is the story of how Tony meets Rudolph (and his sister Anna, who hasn't got her proper teeth yet, so can only drink milk) just as charming as I remember it being, but I'd dare to say it's even better than I had built it up to be in my mind.<br /><br />Some things feel dated, but I think that might be part of its charm.  There's no internet for Tony to go looking up information about vampires, he and his family (and eventually his vampire friends) sit around playing board games together, there's still a late night scary movie on every weekend...it's just a lot of fun.<br /><br />If you are interested in picking up <em>The Little Vampire </em>(for yourself or a younger reader you may know), head over to Open Road for <a href="http://www.openroadmedia.com/the-little-vampire" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">links to booksellers that have the ebook</a>.  It's currently $5 or less at most vendors, which is a pretty darn good deal.<br /><br />I have my fingers crossed that eventually the rest of the books will be re-released and make their way onto my reader.  Thanks again to Open Road Media for the eGalley and to Emily in the Children's Department for answering my questions about the possibility of more releases.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1405135471369867939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842704448" href="/book/show/1367798.The_Little_Vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=1970-1999">1970-1999</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=_europe-western">_europe-western</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530083335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1084452494306870470">The second installment of this popular series, <i>The Little Vampire Moves In</i>, was one of my childhood favourites, and even inspired me to make a vampire cape for a Halloween party. Even though I have read the book countless of times, it's in an excellent shape. I loaned some of the next installments from the library ages ago, but in a random order and I can't remember anything about them anymore. It doesn't really matter that much if you don't read the books in order, but I have an obsession for i</span>
  <span id="freeText1084452494306870470" style="display:none">The second installment of this popular series, <i>The Little Vampire Moves In</i>, was one of my childhood favourites, and even inspired me to make a vampire cape for a Halloween party. Even though I have read the book countless of times, it's in an excellent shape. I loaned some of the next installments from the library ages ago, but in a random order and I can't remember anything about them anymore. It doesn't really matter that much if you don't read the books in order, but I have an obsession for it. I finally wanted to read this first one, and dive into the nostalgic world of the von Schlotterstein vampire family.<br /><br />This did have the familiar magic, although I didn't get the exactly same feeling of excitement that I used to. The series was my first confrontation with vampires, and maybe partly because of this I prefer the traditional vampires that smell like sweaty coffins and soil. Here vampires aren't too tame, as you would think from a children's book, but for example aunt Dorothee still had that creepy air around her. It was interesting to realise that the feeding habits of vampires aren't even once referred to directly as biting. Anton's family is charming, but not ridiculously perfect. Mom gets a tad too curious all the time and dad gets angry easily. A special mention goes to Amelie Glinke's illustrations, which stuck into my mind ever since I saw them for the first time. The delicate gossamer pencil lines fit perfectly for the atmosphere, and the characters to the overall charming character of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1084452494306870470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361414934" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14337587855982529239">This book has a lexile level of 610 and is suited for students in the 3rd grade. The main character is Tony and it's from the 3rd point of view. The setting is in a couple places such as Tony's house and the cemetery. In this book, Tony is a 10 year old who gets bored a lot and doesn't have many friends. One night, when his parents were out, he heard a strange noise coming from his room and realized it was a vampire. Even though he was scared at first, that quickly went away as they developed a </span>
  <span id="freeText14337587855982529239" style="display:none">This book has a lexile level of 610 and is suited for students in the 3rd grade. The main character is Tony and it's from the 3rd point of view. The setting is in a couple places such as Tony's house and the cemetery. In this book, Tony is a 10 year old who gets bored a lot and doesn't have many friends. One night, when his parents were out, he heard a strange noise coming from his room and realized it was a vampire. Even though he was scared at first, that quickly went away as they developed a friendship. Throughout the book, Tony and Rudolph (the vampire's name) go on various adventures by meeting Rudolph's vampire family, seeing his coffin, and more crazy things. The main idea is to have an imagination and for parents to be more open minded about things.<br /><br />I would recommend this book because it gives kids an edge on their seat and a good thrill. It's also a good way to introduce vampires. Overall, I thought the book was a lot of fun to read. I kind of wish I had read this when I was younger because I probably would have enjoyed it a lot more. <br /><br />This is a book I will remember. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8106600671137307203">Picked up one of my favorite childhood books! I still remember a lot of it by heart <3<br/><br/>It's about 9 year-old Anton who's home alone, and suddenly, the little vampire Rydiger von Schlotterstein knocks on his window!   <span id="freeText8106600671137307203" style="display:none">Picked up one of my favorite childhood books! I still remember a lot of it by heart &lt;3<br /><br />It's about 9 year-old Anton who's home alone, and suddenly, the little vampire Rydiger von Schlotterstein knocks on his window! Anton is afraid at first, but they soon become friends. Rydiger brings him a vampire cloak so he can fly, and they visit Rydiger's home, the graveyard - but has to hide from his family members.<br />Of course Anton has to hide all this from his nosy parents, who doesn't believe him even though he tells the truth - but they still want to meet Rydiger and his little sister Anna.<br />This is way too much for a 9 year-old to take!<br /><br />I only own this first book, which isn't very long, but I remember borrowing the series in my elementary school library, and loved them all.<br />I really recommend the whole series for spooky children and vampire-obsessed adults!<br />I'm sure some of you have heard of this series, as it has been around for a good while.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287585189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7365675532114184771">I don't remember any of it now, I just remember loving it as a kid, and wanting to read the next book, and wanting to have a vampire friend, and wanting to become a vampire myself...Probably my fantasy of locking myself inside a coffin with a vampire came from this book too, though I wouldn't know why (Just like I have no idea why I'm letting you know that.)This book opened the doors of my imagination and made me fall in love with vampires with such an undying love that has survived even the Twi</span>
  <span id="freeText7365675532114184771" style="display:none">I don't remember any of it now, I just remember loving it as a kid, and wanting to read the next book, and wanting to have a vampire friend, and wanting to become a vampire myself...Probably my fantasy of locking myself inside a coffin with a vampire came from this book too, though I wouldn't know why (Just like I have no idea why I'm letting you know that.)This book opened the doors of my imagination and made me fall in love with vampires with such an undying love that has survived even the Twilight books. I would love to read this again, and I hope I still have the heart and spirit of a kid to enjoy it as much as I did so many years ago.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2683315410" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683315410" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1560497-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222264967p2/1560497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683315410?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/1560497-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/6560292-my-friend-the-vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1560497-meredith?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1560497-meredith?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683315410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3560131726715459481">One evening a young vampire flies through Tony's window and befriends him.<br/><br/>Alas, my German is too rusty for me to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2564031.Der_kleine_Vampir__Der_kleine_Vampir___1_' title='Der kleine Vampir (Der kleine Vampir, #1) by Angela Sommer-Bodenburg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Der kleine Vampir</a> in the original, so I had to settle for this translation. This is a fun little story. A vampire roughly the same age as the protagonist appears out of nowhere one night, and they form a friendship. This is the type of thing I would have liked to happen to me as a child, and I think I would have enjoyed the story more if I'd read it when I was in upper elementary</span>
  <span id="freeText3560131726715459481" style="display:none">One evening a young vampire flies through Tony's window and befriends him.<br /><br />Alas, my German is too rusty for me to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2564031.Der_kleine_Vampir__Der_kleine_Vampir___1_" title="Der kleine Vampir (Der kleine Vampir, #1) by Angela Sommer-Bodenburg" rel="nofollow noopener">Der kleine Vampir</a> in the original, so I had to settle for this translation. This is a fun little story. A vampire roughly the same age as the protagonist appears out of nowhere one night, and they form a friendship. This is the type of thing I would have liked to happen to me as a child, and I think I would have enjoyed the story more if I'd read it when I was in upper elementary school. (Tony is a 10 year-old 5th grader, and his and Rudolph's exploits are rather benign and completely child appropriate.) <br /><br />The vampires all adhere to traditional vampire lore unless it is inconvenient for the plot such as needing permission to cross the threshold. They are dead, drink blood, and sleep in their original graves. They can fly and turn into bats. They can be killed by having a stake hammered through their hearts, and sunlight is fatal to them. Rudolph's younger sister drinks milk instead of blood because she was so young when she died, which I thought was a cute twist. <br /><br />There's no hidden depth to the story. Although, if the reader wanted to make a stretch, it can possibly be read as a metaphor for cross-cultural friendships as both Tony and Rudolph experience the differences in each other's day-to-day lives. <br /><br />The story is markedly dated as Tony is a latchkey kid whose parents have no qualms about his visiting a friend whose address and phone number he cannot provide and whose parents they have never met or contacted. His parents also leave him home alone on date night. By contemporary standards I found this shocking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3560131726715459481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109679540-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580789563p2/109679540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3175637084?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/109679540-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109679540-nick?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3175637084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10837527812468745027">This is SUCH an underrated series, and even though it's aimed at children, adults can enjoy it too. I read it when I was a young teen and I was obsessed with this vampire family. Definitely recommend it for kids who aren't avid readers, these characters are so endearing and so very German. It's a blast.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999001263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17788162672424650785">It does not have Harry Potter's massive appeal for adult readers, but it has a lot of charm and it's a wonderful classic of children's literature. The story of a young boy who makes friends with a boy vampire has funny moments and moments of danger. It's told in a very colloquial and readable way.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('goQUxHKAbxAIzpxxmQj7f/6RNgx6YEU4yQOPQ4WZ+1HEwJdfCOpKCxdfKn3XDQrvV5WgvG0sJhP94PhhOnaGEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1DUMg/8g4JPsEX2DBBjr7jFPu0F0u3YF7PEBKMGhiX6ScY8YhUrFiPOAy49KHRp+mEst8WP3FS7YEnYKfk70Pg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/35595.Angela_Sommer_Bodenburg">About Angela Sommer-Bodenburg</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14469516052648853081">Angela Sommer-Bodenburg is the author of a number of fantasy books for children. Her most famous contribution to the field of children's fantasy is "The Little Vampire" series which has sold over 10 million copies and has been translated into over 30 languages. Sommer-Bodenburg states that her "vampire is not a bloodthirsty monster, however, but an affectionate little vampire with fears and foible</span>
  <span id="freeText14469516052648853081" style="display:none">Angela Sommer-Bodenburg is the author of a number of fantasy books for children. Her most famous contribution to the field of children's fantasy is "The Little Vampire" series which has sold over 10 million copies and has been translated into over 30 languages. Sommer-Bodenburg states that her "vampire is not a bloodthirsty monster, however, but an affectionate little vampire with fears and foibles who will perhaps help free children of their own fears." The novel, written in 1979, spawned a series of books, and the plot has been adapted to theatre, radio, cinema, and television. A Canadian-German TV series was released in 1986 and a film version, directed by Uli Edel was released in 2000.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14469516052648853081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
